	      &= \ham_\text{eff}\ket{\psi_1}
\eeq
We can evaluate the effective Hamiltonian.
\beq
\ham_\text{eff} &= \ham_0 + \epsilon_d + V_{0 \to 1}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0}V_{1\to 0} + V_{2 \to 1}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - 2\epsilon_d - U}V_{1\to 2}\\
\eeq
The first renormalization term gives
\beq
V_{0 \to 1}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0}V_{1\to 0} = \sum_{kq\sigma\alpha}V_k^*V_qc^\dagger_{d\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\rr{1 - \hat n_{d\ol\sigma}}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0} c^\dagger_{q\gamma}c_{d\gamma}\rr{1 - \hat n_{d\ol\gamma}}
\eeq
We can \textit{approximate} \(E\) by replacing it with the bare energy of \(\ket{\psi_1}\): \(E = \ham_0 - \epsilon_q + \epsilon_d\).
\beq
V_{0 \to 1}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0}V_{1\to 0} = \sum_{kq\sigma\gamma}V_k^*V_qc^\dagger_{d\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\rr{1 - \hat n_{d\ol\sigma}}c^\dagger_{q\gamma}c_{d\gamma}\rr{1 - \hat n_{d\ol\gamma}}\frac{1}{\epsilon_d - \epsilon_q}
\eeq
Similarly, the second term becomes
\beq
V_{2 \to 1}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - 2\epsilon_d - U}V_{1\to 2} = \sum_{kq\sigma\gamma}V_k^*V_qc^\dagger_{q\gamma}c_{d\gamma}\hat n_{d\ol\gamma}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - 2\epsilon_d - U}c^\dagger_{d\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\hat n_{d\ol\sigma}
\eeq
We again approximate \(E\): \(E = \ham_0 + \epsilon_k - \epsilon_d\):
\beq
V_{2 \to 1}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - 2\epsilon_d - U}V_{1\to 2} = \sum_{kq\sigma\gamma}V_k^*V_qc^\dagger_{q\gamma}c_{d\gamma}\hat n_{d\ol\gamma}c^\dagger_{d\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\hat n_{d\ol\sigma}\frac{1}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d - U}
\eeq
The sum of these two terms give the total renormalization. First we look at those terms where \(\gamma=\sigma\). The total renormalization from that part is
\beq
\sum_{kq\sigma}V_k^*V_q\qq{\frac{\hat n_{d\sigma}\rr{1 - \hat n_{d\ol\sigma}}c_{k\sigma}c^\dagger_{q\sigma}}{\epsilon_d - \epsilon_q} + \frac{\rr{1 - \hat n_{d\sigma}}\hat n_{d\ol\sigma}c^\dagger_{q\sigma}c_{k\sigma}}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d - U}} &= \sum_{kq\sigma}V_k^*V_q\qq{\frac{\hat n_{d\sigma}c_{k\sigma}c^\dagger_{q\sigma}}{\epsilon_d - \epsilon_q} + \frac{\hat n_{d\ol\sigma}c^\dagger_{q\sigma}c_{k\sigma}}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d - U}}\\
&= \sum_{kq\sigma}V_k^*V_q\qq{\frac{\hat n_{d\sigma}c^\dagger_{q\sigma}c_{k\sigma}}{\epsilon_q - \epsilon_d} + \frac{\hat n_{d\ol\sigma}c^\dagger_{q\sigma}c_{k\sigma}}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d - U}}
\eeq
In the first step we used \(\hat n_{\sigma}\hat n_{d\ol\sigma}=0\) because we are in the single-occupied subspace and in the second step we used \(c_{k\sigma}c^\dagger_{q\sigma} = \delta_{kq} - c^\dagger_{q\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\) and dropped the constant \(\delta\) part. We can now write this this thing in terms of spin operator \(S_d^z = \hf\sigma\rr{\hat n_{d\sigma} - \hat n_{d\ol\sigma}}\) and also use \(\hat n_{\sigma} + \hat n_{\ol\sigma} = 1\). They give
\beq
&\sum_{kq\sigma}V_k^*V_q\qq{\frac{\rr{\hf + \sigma S_d^z}c^\dagger_{q\sigma}c_{k\sigma}}{\epsilon_q - \epsilon_d} + \frac{\rr{\hf - \sigma S_d^z}c^\dagger_{q\sigma}c_{k\sigma}}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d - U}}\\
&= \sum_{kq\sigma}V_k^*V_qS_d^z \sigma c^\dagger_{q\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\qq{\frac{1}{\epsilon_q - \epsilon_d} - \frac{1}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d - U}} + \hf\sum_{kq\sigma}V_k^*V_qc^\dagger_{q\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\qq{\frac{1}{\epsilon_q - \epsilon_d} + \frac{1}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d - U}}
\eeq
The latter term is a potential scattering term; it vanishes in the particle-hole symmetric case (\(\epsilon_d + U = -\epsilon_d\)) and we will ignore it from now. The first term is the gives rise to the spin-preserving scattering in the s-d model; we can write \(\sum_\sigma\sigma c^\dagger_{q\sigma}c_{k\sigma} = c^\dagger_{q\ua}c_{k\ua} - c^\dagger_{q\da}c_{k\da} \equiv 2s^z_{kq}\). Defining \(J_{kq} = V_k^*V_q\qq{\frac{1}{\epsilon_q - \epsilon_d} - \frac{1}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d - U}}\), gives us the first term in s-d model
\beq
2\sum_{kq}J_{kq} S_d^z s^z_{kq}
\eeq
Setting \(\gamma = \ol\sigma\) in the total renormalization gives the rest of the terms:
\beq
\sum_{kq\sigma}V_k^*V_qc^\dagger_{d\sigma}c_{d\ol\sigma}c^\dagger_{q\ol\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\qq{\frac{-1}{\epsilon_d - \epsilon_q} + \frac{-1}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d - U}} =\sum_{kq\sigma}J_{kq}c^\dagger_{d\sigma}c_{d\ol\sigma}c^\dagger_{q\ol\sigma}c_{k\sigma}
\eeq
We can define \(S_d^\sigma = c^\dagger_{d\sigma}c_{d\ol\sigma}\) where \(\sigma \in \cc{+,-}\) and \(s^{\ol\sigma}_{kq} = c^\dagger_{q\ol\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\). This gives
\beq
\sum_{kq\sigma}J_{kq}S_d^\sigma s_{kq}^{\ol\sigma} = \sum_{kq}J_{kq}\rr{S_d^+ s_{kq}^- + S_d^- s_{kq}^+}
\eeq
The total renormalization, minus the potential scattering and constant terms constitutes the spin-flip scattering part of the Kondo model:
\beq
\ham_{s-d} = 2\sum_{kq}J_{kq}\qq{S_d^z s^z_{kq} + \hf\rr{S_d^+ s_{kq}^- + S_d^- s_{kq}^+}} = 2\sum_{kq}J_{kq}\vec{S}_d\cdot\vec{s}_{kq}
\eeq
Note that when we wrote the entire Schrodinger equation in the subspace of \(\ket{\psi_1}\), we projected out all contributions of the Hamiltonian in the subspace of the doublon and holon. To recover those parts, we can look at eq.~\ref{sceq} by eliminating \(\ket{\psi_1}\). That gives
\beq
E\ket{\psi_0} &= \rr{\ham_0 + V_{1 \to 0}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_{0\to 1}}\ket{\psi_0} + V_{1 \to 0}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_{2\to 1}\psi_2\\
E\ket{\psi_2} &= \rr{\ham_0 + 2\epsilon_d + U + V_{1\to 2}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_{2\to 1}}\ket{\psi_2} + V_{1\to 2}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_{0\to 1}\psi_0\\
\eeq
It can be represented in the matrix form:
\beq
\begin{pmatrix} \ham_0 + V_{1 \to 0}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_{0\to 1} & V_{1 \to 0}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_{2\to 1} \\\\ V_{1\to 2}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_{0\to 1} & \ham_0 + 2\epsilon_d + U + V_{1\to 2}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_{2\to 1} \end{pmatrix} \begin{pmatrix} \psi_0 \\\\ \psi_2 \end{pmatrix} = E \begin{pmatrix} \psi_0 \\\\ \psi_2 \end{pmatrix}
\eeq
There are two scattering terms in each equation. The first scattering term (of the forms \(V_{1 \to 0}GV_{0\to 1}\) and \(V_{1 \to 2}GV_{2\to 1}\)) involve virtual excitations to the single-occupied subspace. They are diagonal in their respective subspaces. However, \textit{the second scattering term in each equation, of the form \(V_{1 \to 0}GV_{2\to 1}\) or \(V_{1 \to 2}GV_{0\to 1}\) scatter between the doublon and holon subspace.} The first one takes you from the doublon to the holon (\(2 \to 1 \to 0\)), the second one does the oppposte. Let us take a look at these terms. The first term becomes
\beq
V_{1 \to 0}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_{2\to 1} &= \sum_{kq\sigma\gamma}V_q c^\dagger_{q\gamma}c_{d\gamma}\rr{1 - \hat n_{d\ol\gamma}}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_k c^\dagger_{k\sigma}c_{d\sigma}\hat n_{d\ol\sigma}\\
						       &=\sum_{kq\sigma\gamma}V_q c^\dagger_{q\gamma}c_{d\gamma}\rr{1 - \hat n_{d\ol\gamma}}V_k c^\dagger_{k\sigma}c_{d\sigma}\hat n_{d\ol\sigma}\frac{1}{\epsilon_d + U - \epsilon_k}
\eeq
where I put \(E = \ham_0 - \epsilon_k + 2\epsilon_d + U\) as the energy of the initial state \(\ket{\psi_2}\). Since the expression has \(c_{d\gamma}\) followed by \(c_{d\sigma}\) with only diagonal terms in between, we must have \(\gamma = \ol\sigma\). Hence it becomes
\beq
\sum_{kq\sigma}V_qV_k c^\dagger_{q\ol\sigma}c_{d\ol\sigma}c^\dagger_{k\sigma}c_{d\sigma}\frac{1}{\epsilon_d + U - \epsilon_k} &= \sum_{kq}V_q V_k\frac{1}{\epsilon_d + U - \epsilon_k}\qq{c^\dagger_{q\ua}c^\dagger_{k\da}c_{d\da}c_{d\ua} + c^\dagger_{q\da}c^\dagger_{k\ua}c_{d\ua}c_{d\da}}\\
&= \sum_{kq}V_q V_k\frac{1}{\epsilon_d + U - \epsilon_k}\qq{c^\dagger_{q\ua}c^\dagger_{k\da}c_{d\da}c_{d\ua} + c^\dagger_{k\ua}c^\dagger_{q\da}c_{d\da}c_{d\ua}}\\
&= \sum_{kq}V_q V_kc^\dagger_{q\ua}c^\dagger_{k\da}c_{d\da}c_{d\ua}\rr{\frac{1}{\epsilon_d + U - \epsilon_k} + \frac{1}{\epsilon_d + U - \epsilon_q}}
\eeq
In the last step, we relabeled \(k \leftrightarrow q\). The second scattering term similarly becomes
\beq
V_{1 \to 2}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_{0\to 1} &= \sum_{kq\sigma\gamma}V_q^* c^\dagger_{d\gamma}c_{q\gamma}\hat n_{d\ol\gamma}\frac{1}{E - \ham_0 - \epsilon_d}V_k^* c^\dagger_{d\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\rr{1 - \hat n_{d\ol\sigma}}\\
						       &=\sum_{kq\sigma}V_q^*V_k^* c^\dagger_{d\ol\sigma}c_{q\ol\sigma} c^\dagger_{d\sigma}c_{k\sigma}\frac{1}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d}\\
						       &=\sum_{kq}V_q^*V_k^* \rr{\frac{1}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d} + \frac{1}{\epsilon_q - \epsilon_d}}c^\dagger_{d\ua}c^\dagger_{d\da}c_{k\da}c_{q\ua}
\eeq
Combining the two terms, we get the total charge-Kondo contribution:
\beq
\ham_{ch} = \sum_{kq}V_q V_kc^\dagger_{q\ua}c^\dagger_{k\da}c_{d\da}c_{d\ua}\rr{\frac{1}{\epsilon_d + U - \epsilon_k} + \frac{1}{\epsilon_d + U - \epsilon_q}} \\
+ \sum_{kq}V_q^*V_k^*c^\dagger_{d\ua}c^\dagger_{d\da}c_{k\da}c_{q\ua}\rr{\frac{1}{\epsilon_k - \epsilon_d} + \frac{1}{\epsilon_q - \epsilon_d}}
\eeq
}
%}
\subsection{CUT RG}
In CUT (continuous unitary transformation) RG \cite{glazek-wilson}, we progressively block-diagonalize the Hamiltonian by removing off-diagonal terms that are farthest from the diagonal, through infinitesimal unitary transformations. The change is described as a flow against some parameter \(\lambda\) of the Hamiltonian. Denoting the unitary transformation generator by \(Sd\lambda\) for a change \(d\lambda\), we can write
\beq
H (\lambda + d\lambda) = e^{Sd\lambda} \ham(\lambda) e^{-Sd\lambda} \approx \rr{1 + Sd\lambda}\ham(\lambda) \rr{1 - Sd\lambda}\\
= \ham(\lambda) + d\lambda\qq{S,\ham(\lambda)} + O(d\lambda^2)
\eeq
Formally taking the limit of \(d\lambda \to 0\) gives
\beq
\dv{\ham(\lambda)}{\lambda} = \qq{S,\ham(\lambda)}
\eeq
In CUT RG, we choose the generator as \(S = \qq{\ham_d,\ham_X}\), where \(\ham_d\) is the diagonal part of the Hamiltonian and \(\ham_X = \ham - \ham_d\) is the off-diagonal part of the Hamiltonian. Therefore,
\beq[cut]
\dv{\ham}{\lambda} = \qq{\qq{\ham_d,\ham_X},\ham}
\eeq
We will now see that the renormalization in URG can also be put into a similar form. From eq.~\ref{renurg}, we can write the URG renormalization as
\beq
\Delta \ham = \hf\qq{\eta^\dagger - \eta,\ham}
\eeq
The URG generator can be recast (starting from the definitions of \(\eta\), eqs.~\ref{etadefine}) as
\beq
\eta^\dagger - \eta &= G_1 c^\dagger T - G_0 T^\dagger c\\
		    &= \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}\qq{G_1 \rr{\omega_1 - \omega_0}c^\dagger T - G_0 \rr{\omega_1 - \omega_0}T^\dagger c}\\
		    &= \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}\qq{G_1 \omega_1 c^\dagger T - c^\dagger T\omega_0G_0 - T^\dagger c \omega_1 G_1 +  G_0\omega_0T^\dagger c}\\
\eeq
In the last step, we changed the second and fourth terms using the constraints \(G_1 c^\dagger T = c^\dagger T G_0\) and \(G_0 T^\dagger c = T^\dagger c G_1\), eq.~\ref{constraint}. We now add and subtract \(G_1 G_1^{-1}c^\dagger T = c^\dagger T\) and \(G_0 G_0^{-1}T^\dagger c = T^\dagger c\) for each term.
\beq
\eta^\dagger - \eta = \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}&\left[G_1 \rr{\omega_1 - G_1^{-1}}c^\dagger T + c^\dagger T - c^\dagger T \rr{\omega_0 - G_0^{-1}} G_0 - c^\dagger T \right.\\
						   &\left.-  T^\dagger c\rr{\omega_1 - G_1^{-1}}G_1 - T^\dagger c +  G_0\rr{\omega_0 - G_0^{-1}}T^\dagger c + T^\dagger c\right]\\
= \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}&\left[G_1 \rr{\omega_1 - G_1^{-1}}c^\dagger T - c^\dagger T \rr{\omega_0 - G_0^{-1}} G_0 \right.\\
&\left.-  T^\dagger c\rr{\omega_1 - G_1^{-1}}G_1 +  G_0\rr{\omega_0 - G_0^{-1}}T^\dagger c\right]\\
\eeq
In the last step, the extra \(c^\dagger T\) and \(T^\dagger c\) terms canceled out. In the second and third terms, we can bring the Greens function closer to the operators \(c^\dagger T\) and \(T^\dagger c\) because \(\rr{\omega_j - G_j^{-1}}G_j = G_j\rr{\omega_j - G_j^{-1}}\):
\beq
\eta^\dagger - \eta = \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}&\left[G_1 \rr{\omega_1 - G_1^{-1}}c^\dagger T - c^\dagger T G_0 \rr{\omega_0 - G_0^{-1}} \right.\\
&\left.-  T^\dagger cG_1\rr{\omega_1 - G_1^{-1}} +  G_0\rr{\omega_0 - G_0^{-1}}T^\dagger c\right]\\
= \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}&\left[G_1 \rr{\omega_1 - G_1^{-1}}c^\dagger T - G_1c^\dagger T  \rr{\omega_0 - G_0^{-1}} \right.\\
&\left.-  G_0T^\dagger c\rr{\omega_1 - G_1^{-1}} +  G_0\rr{\omega_0 - G_0^{-1}}T^\dagger c\right]\\
\eeq
In the last step, we again used the constraint \(G_1 c^\dagger T = c^\dagger T G_0\) and its partner. From the definition of the Green's function \(G = \rr{\omega - \ham^d}^{-1}\), we can write \(\omega_j - G_j^{-1} = \ham^d_j\). Therefore,
\beq
\eta^\dagger - \eta = \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}&\left[G_1 \ham^d_1 c^\dagger T - G_1c^\dagger T \ham^d_0  -  G_0 T^\dagger c \ham^d_1 +  G_0 \ham^d_0 T^\dagger c\right]\\
= \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}&\left[G \ham^d c^\dagger T - Gc^\dagger T \ham^d  -  G T^\dagger c \ham^d +  G \ham^d T^\dagger c\right]\\
= \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}&G\qq{ \ham^d, c^\dagger T + T^\dagger c}\\
\eeq
where \(\ham^d = \ham^d_1 \hat n + \ham^d_0 \rr{1 - \hat n}\) and \(G = G_1 \hat n + G_0 \rr{1 -\hat n} = \rr{\hat \omega - \ham^d}^{-1}\). For URG, the relevant off-diagonal part of the Hamiltonian for the current node is \(\ham^I = c^\dagger T + T^\dagger c\). Therefore,
\beq
\eta^\dagger - \eta = \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}G\qq{ \ham^d, \ham^I}\\
\eeq
The renormalization in the Hamiltonian under URG, which is a function of both the quantum fluctuation scale \(\omega\) and the running bandwidth \(D\), can thus be written as
\beq
\Delta \ham (\omega,D) =  \frac{1}{\omega_1 - \omega_0}\qq{G\qq{ \ham^d, \ham^I},\ham}\\
\eeq
This can be compared to the analogous equation for CUT (eq.~\ref{cut}),
\beq
\Delta{\ham}(\lambda) = \Delta{\lambda}\qq{\qq{\ham_d,\ham_X},\ham}
\eeq
Leaving aside the obvious differences in the philosophies (the presence of \(\omega\) in URG or the fact that while URG decouples as a flow in the bandwidth, CUT uses a general parameter \(\lambda\) or the algorithmic difference that while URG decouples one specific node, CUT tries to make the Hamiltonian band-diagonal), the major physical difference is the presence of the total Green's function in the URG equation. It must be noted that while CUT employs the entire off-diagonal part in \(\ham_X\), the \(\ham^I\) of URG contains only those parts that are off-diagonal with respect to the node being decoupled at this step. To bring the URG form closer to CUT, we can make some approximations. 
\beq
G c^\dagger T = G_1 c^\dagger T = \fr{1}{\omega_1 - \ham^d_1}c^\dagger T \approx -\fr{1}{\ham^d_1}c^\dagger T
\eeq
where we dropped \(\omega_1\) for small quantum fluctuations. Similarly,
\beq
G T^\dagger c = G_0 T^\dagger c = T^\dagger c \fr{1}{\omega_1 - \ham^d_1}\approx -\fr{1}{\ham^d_1}T^\dagger c
\eeq
This gives
\beq
\Delta \ham (\omega,D) =  \frac{1}{\ham^d_1}\frac{1}{\omega_0 - \omega_1}\qq{\qq{ \ham^d, \ham^I},\ham}
\eeq
We can thus make the connection,
\beq
\Delta \lambda \sim \frac{1}{\ham^d_1}\frac{1}{\omega_0 - \omega_1}
\eeq
